<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>PART I    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="de1898_item_1._business"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_de1898_2"> </A></FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>ITEM 1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;BUSINESS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Except where otherwise noted, the words "we," "us," "our," and similar terms, as well as references to "Argosy" or the "Company" refer to Argosy Gaming Company
and all of its subsidiaries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>The Company  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We are a leading owner and operator of six riverboat casinos located in the central United States. We pioneered riverboat gaming in St. Louis, Kansas City and
Baton Rouge by opening the first casino in each of those markets. Our riverboat casino that serves the Cincinnati market from Lawrenceburg, Indiana is one of the largest revenue producing riverboats
in the United States gaming industry. In addition, we own the Empress Casino Joliet serving the Chicago, Illinois market. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
are a Delaware corporation. Our principal executive offices are located at 219 Piasa Street, Alton, Illinois 62002 and our telephone number is (618)&nbsp;474-7500. We
file annual reports on Form&nbsp;10-K, quarterly reports on Form&nbsp;10-Q, current reports on Form&nbsp;8-K, proxy statements, special reports and other
information with the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) and are made available on the SEC's website at </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>www.sec.gov</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and on our website at </FONT> <FONT
SIZE=2><I>www.argosycasinos.com</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, as soon as reasonably practicable after we electronically file such material with, or furnish it to, the SEC. The information
contained on our website is not being incorporated herein. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
following summarizes our casino properties: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
operating strategy emphasizes increasing revenues and profits through enhancing our customers' gaming experience by providing superior service, expanding and refining direct
marketing programs utilizing an extensive customer database, investing in state-of-the-art gaming products, upgrading and renovating our properties and managing
costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Strategy  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;By capitalizing on the extensive gaming industry experience of our management team, we have developed a strategy to maximize the performance of our operating
assets and improve financial results. We continue to implement changes at each of our properties to improve our competitive position, increase gaming revenues and enhance profitability. The key
elements of our business strategy
include: (1)&nbsp;providing our customers a superior gaming experience to foster customer loyalty; (2)&nbsp;focusing on our most valuable customers to encourage repeat business;
(3)&nbsp;enhancing the gaming product at our casinos by investing in state-of-the-art gaming equipment; (4)&nbsp;renovating our properties to create more
exciting gaming environments and (5)&nbsp;pursuing high-return business opportunities. </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Provide our customers with a superior entertainment experience.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;We operate casinos catering to
"locals" customers who generally live within an hour's drive of our casinos. Based on our surveys, our regular customers game an average of three times a month, unlike a destination gaming market,
such as the Las Vegas strip, where people visit less frequently. We believe that </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>1</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=2,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=517079,FOLIO='1',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DE1898A.;16',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_de1898_1_2"> </A>
<UL>
<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>exceptional
customer service and an enjoyable gaming experience are critical to fostering customer loyalty. Our customers have indicated in surveys that cleanliness, a comfortable atmosphere,
attentive staff, availability of games, and a feeling of fun and excitement are important factors that attract them to our casinos. We take our customers' preferences into account when implementing
our operating and capital spending plans. We generally allocate approximately 70% of our maintenance capital expenditures at each property to address issues of importance to customers, with the
majority spent to keep our gaming product fresh and the excitement high. </FONT></P>

</UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Focus on our most valuable customers.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Our primary marketing focus is through direct and
relationship marketing to encourage repeat business with our frequent customers. We use sophisticated player tracking systems to identify and reward premium players and our most loyal customers. Based
on a player's gaming activity, we create promotions including targeted direct mail coin offers and "members only" concerts, parties, tournaments, sweepstakes and special entertainment events. We
employ an integrated data warehouse to expand and refine our knowledge of our customers.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Invest in new gaming equipment.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Slot machines contributed approximately 85% of our casino
revenues in 2002 and are an important element of our profitability. We continually upgrade our gaming product with state-of-the-art slot machines. We believe that
regularly replacing slot machines with the most popular products creates a more exciting gaming experience and increases profitability. During 2003 and 2004, subject to regulatory approvals, we plan
on insuring our entire slot product has cashless ticket-in, ticket-out slot capability. In order to complete our conversion to cashless slot product, Illinois and Louisiana
must first approve cashless slots.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Renovate our riverboat and dockside entertainment facilities.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;To maintain an exciting gaming
experience for our customers, we have developed a capital investment plan to systematically renovate and improve our casino and entertainment facilities in response to customer preferences and market
opportunities. For example, we plan to spend approximately $40&nbsp;million in 2003 to maintain a quality environment for our customers. In addition, we plan on spending approximately
$115&nbsp;million in 2003 to expand our Kansas City, Joliet and Sioux City casinos. The Kansas City and Joliet casinos will become barge-based operations, which our customers find more desirable. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>
<UL>
<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
Riverside, we are looking to replace our current three-level riverboat facility with a single level, 58,000 square-foot barge-based facility, providing for a 50% increase in gaming
positions and a new high limit area. The project will also include the renovation and expansion of the current pavilion to include a new VIP club, new dining venues, an expanded buffet and dining
room, and additional surface and VIP parking areas. We expect to complete this project at the end of 2003, at a total cost of approximately $105&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
Joliet, we will replace our two multi-level riverboat casinos that currently operate a total of five levels of gaming space with a two-level barge purchased in 2002. The barge is
undergoing extensive renovations and will offer approximately 50,000 square feet of gaming space, plus an additional 15,000 square feet for a party room and player's lounge. The project is targeted to
open in the second quarter 2003 at a total cost of approximately $40&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

</UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Pursue strategic opportunities and acquisitions that provide superior returns.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;We look to invest
in growth opportunities that add shareholder value while maintaining an appropriate capital structure. Our acquisition of the Empress Casino Joliet during 2001 has increased and diversified our cash
flow within the largest locals gaming market and third largest gaming market in the United States. In the future, we will continue to evaluate and pursue possible acquisitions of complementary
businesses and other strategic opportunities to enhance shareholder value. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>2</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=3,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=972994,FOLIO='2',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DE1898A.;16',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_de1898_1_3"> </A>
<UL>
<UL>
</UL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Casino Properties  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Argosy Casino Lawrenceburg  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Lawrenceburg casino is located on the Ohio River in Lawrenceburg, Indiana approximately 15 miles west of
Cincinnati and is the closest casino to the Cincinnati metropolitan area. The Lawrenceburg casino is one of the largest riverboats in the United States with 74,300 square feet of gaming space on three
levels with 2,143 slot machines and 94 table games. In 2002, the Indiana gaming commission approved dockside gaming and our Lawrenceburg casino commenced dockside gaming on August&nbsp;1, 2002. As
such, our Lawrenceburg casino no longer cruises. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
complex also features a 300 room hotel, a 200,000 square foot land-based entertainment pavilion and support facility offering a 350 seat buffet restaurant, two specialty
restaurants, an entertainment lounge and an 1,800 space parking garage. Employee and overflow parking is provided at a 1,400 space remote lot that is accessed by shuttle bus. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital Improvements:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 2002, we spent approximately $8.3&nbsp;million on capital improvements consisting entirely of
maintenance capital. In 2003, we intend to spend approximately $8&nbsp;million on capital improvements, including $5&nbsp;million related to cashless gaming products. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gaming Market:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Lawrenceburg casino draws from a population of approximately 1.6&nbsp;million residents in the
Cincinnati metropolitan area and an additional 5.4&nbsp;million people who reside within 100 miles of Lawrenceburg, including the major metropolitan markets of Dayton and Columbus, Ohio and, to a
lesser extent, Indianapolis, Indiana and Lexington, Kentucky. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
the Cincinnati market, the Lawrenceburg casino directly competes with two other riverboat casinos. The three riverboat casinos operating in the Cincinnati market generated
$626.9&nbsp;million of gaming revenues in 2002, a 9.3% increase from 2001. In 2002, the Lawrenceburg casino represented 45.1% of gaming position capacity in the Cincinnati market, and captured 59.6%
of the market's gaming revenues. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Lawrenceburg casino is the closest casino to the Cincinnati metropolitan area. Our nearest competitor is located approximately 15 miles further south of Lawrenceburg in Rising Sun,
Indiana. Another competitor is located 40 miles from Lawrenceburg in Switzerland County, Indiana. Secondarily, we compete with a riverboat casino in Bridgeport, Indiana in the Louisville, Kentucky
area approximately 100 miles from Lawrenceburg. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulatory Update:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Indiana gaming law currently limits the number of gaming licenses to be issued in the state to a total of
11, including a maximum of 5 licenses and a limit of one license per county along the Ohio River. Indiana gaming law does not restrict the size of a licensee's gaming facility or place limits on
customer losses or betting levels. Our Indiana gaming license is subject to renewal on an annual basis. Effective August&nbsp;1, 2002, our casino commenced dockside gaming allowing our customers
continuous unlimited ingress and egress during its hours of operation and no longer requiring cruises. At the same time, Indiana enacted legislation to increase gaming tax rates for those casinos
adopting dockside gaming. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Casino
gaming is not currently permitted under the laws of either Ohio or Kentucky. The Ohio legislature has considered, at various times, legislation that would allow certain types of
casino-style gaming at Ohio racetracks. Legislation has been introduced to allow Kentucky racetracks to have slot machines. The Kentucky legislation would allow any kind of electronic games, from
slots to keno to video poker as well as wide area progressives. The Indiana legislature has considered, at various times, additional legislation that could apply certain provisions of tax increases
enacted during 2002 on a retro-active basis and also proposed to eliminate the existing restrictions on owning more than one
Indiana casino and allows each county with riverboat gaming to hold a referendum to allow dockside gaming. To date, Ohio, Kentucky and Indiana have not enacted such proposed legislation. Enactment </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>3</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=4,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=45038,FOLIO='3',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DE1898A.;16',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_de1898_1_4"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
of such legislation by Ohio, Kentucky or Indiana could have an adverse affect on the financial results of our Lawrenceburg casino. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Alton Belle Casino  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Alton Belle Casino is located on the Mississippi River in Alton, Illinois approximately 20 miles northeast of
downtown St. Louis. We commenced operations in Alton, Illinois in September&nbsp;1991 as the first gaming facility in Illinois and the St. Louis metropolitan market. Following the success of our
original Alton riverboat casino, we built and opened a larger three-deck contemporary style cruise liner. The cruise liner features 26,700 square feet of gaming space, 1,013 slot machines
and 28 table games. In June&nbsp;1999, Illinois passed a law permitting casinos to offer continuous dockside gaming. As a result, the Alton Belle Casino remains dockside and offers its customers
unlimited ingress and egress during its hours of operation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Alton property includes an approximately 60,000 square foot entertainment pavilion and features a 124 seat buffet, a restaurant and a 400 seat main showroom. Parking is available at
an adjacent city-owned surface parking facility and at two sites in the city of Alton, to and from which we provide valet parking as well as free shuttle service. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital Improvements:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 2002, we spent approximately $2.8&nbsp;million on capital improvements, including
$2.2&nbsp;million on maintenance capital. In 2003, we intend to spend approximately $3&nbsp;million on capital improvements, including $2&nbsp;million on cashless gaming products subject to
approval of such products in Illinois. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gaming Market:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Alton Belle Casino generally draws from a population of approximately 2.5&nbsp;million residents within
the St. Louis metropolitan area and an additional 1.2&nbsp;million people within a 100-mile radius of the City of St. Louis. The target customers of the Alton Belle Casino are drawn
largely from the northern and eastern regions of the greater St. Louis metropolitan area, as well as portions of central and southern Illinois. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Alton Belle Casino faces competition from four other riverboat casino companies currently operating in the St. Louis area, including one other Illinois licensee. As an Illinois
licensee, the Alton Belle Casino is not subject to Missouri's $500 loss limit and therefore has a competitive advantage in attracting high-end customers over the three competitors
operating under Missouri licenses. The
riverboat casinos operating in the St. Louis market generated $804.5&nbsp;million of gaming revenues in 2002, a 5.0% increase from 2001. The Alton Belle Casino represented approximately 12.3% of
gaming position capacity in the St. Louis market, and captured approximately 14.8% of the market's gaming revenues. One competitor in Missouri completed a major renovation of its facility in
August&nbsp;2002 that increased the market capacity by 17%. Following this major renovation, the Alton Belle Casino's revenues declined approximately 5% with a corresponding decrease in market
share. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulatory Update:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Illinois gaming law currently limits the number of gaming licenses to be issued in the state to ten. Each
license permits the operation of up to two boats as part of a single riverboat gaming operation with a combined maximum of 1,200 gaming positions as defined by the state. Our Illinois gaming license
is subject to renewal in October&nbsp;2003. During the second quarter 2002, Illinois enacted legislation increasing gaming and admission tax rates. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
June&nbsp;1999, Illinois passed an amendment to the Illinois Riverboat Gambling Act to permit casinos to offer continuous dockside gaming with unlimited ingress and egress. As a
result of litigation challenging certain provisions of the 1999 amendment, dockside gaming could be overturned and we could be required to suspend dockside gaming activities at our Alton casino until
such time as the Illinois legislature reauthorized dockside gaming. We are unable to determine what the ultimate resolution of the litigation will be; however, the loss of dockside gaming at our Alton
casino would adversely affect our financial results. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Argosy Casino Riverside  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Argosy Casino Riverside is located on the Missouri River in Riverside, Missouri on a 55-acre site
approximately five miles from downtown Kansas City. The riverboat features approximately 36,000 square feet of gaming space, 1,131 slot machines and 30 table games. The Kansas City casino began
operations in Kansas City, Missouri on June&nbsp;22, 1994, as the first gaming facility to open in the Kansas City market. During November&nbsp;1999, Missouri adopted open boarding, allowing
customers unlimited ingress and egress, eliminating the two-hour mock cruising requirements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Kansas City casino is complemented by an 85,000 square foot land-based entertainment facility featuring specialty and buffet restaurants, a sports/entertainment lounge
and 8,000 square feet of banquet/conference facilities. A parking garage and surface parking areas with 2,000 spaces are located adjacent to the pavilion. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital Improvements:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During 2002, we spent $13.1&nbsp;million on capital improvements, including $10.1&nbsp;million on
our major renovation project. In 2003, we intend to spend approximately $105&nbsp;million on capital improvements, including completion of our major renovation and conversion to cashless gaming
products. The targeted opening of our new barge-based casino is currently planned by year-end 2003. The new project will allow us to replace our existing three-level riverboat facility
with a single level 58,000 square-foot barge-based facility providing for a 50% increase in gaming positions and a new high limit area. The project also includes the renovation and
expansion of the existing pavilion to include a new VIP club, new dining venues, an expanded buffet and dining room, and additional surface and VIP parking. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gaming Market:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Kansas City casino draws from a population of approximately 1.6&nbsp;million residents in the greater
Kansas City metropolitan area and an additional 900,000 people within a 100-mile radius of Kansas City. The Kansas City casino site offers convenient access from two major highways. The
Kansas City casino primarily attracts customers who reside in the northern and western regions of the Kansas City metropolitan area. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
currently face competition from three other casinos in the Kansas City area. The four riverboat casinos operating in the Kansas City market generated $614.0&nbsp;million of gaming
revenues in 2002, a 5.5% increase from 2001. Our Kansas City casino represented 15.5% of gaming position capacity in the Kansas City market and captured 16.0% of the market's gaming revenues. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulatory Update:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our Missouri gaming license is subject to renewal in June&nbsp;2004 and again every two years
thereafter. Legislation has been filed in Kansas, which, if enacted, would allow for slot machines at racetracks. Missouri has discussed possible increases in admission and gaming taxes. Should Kansas
enact such legislation or Missouri increase admission or gaming taxes, our Kansas City casino's financial results would be adversely affected. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Argosy Casino Baton Rouge  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Argosy Casino Baton Rouge is located on the Mississippi River in downtown Baton Rouge, Louisiana. The riverboat
features approximately 28,000 square feet of gaming space, 877 slot machines and 31 table games. The Baton Rouge casino began operations in September&nbsp;1994 as the first riverboat gaming facility
in the Baton Rouge market. Louisiana adopted legislation effective April&nbsp;1, 2001, that permits dockside gaming, allowing customers unlimited ingress and egress, and eliminating the
three-hour cruising requirements. This legislation also increased the tax on riverboat operations from 18.5% to 21.5%. As a result, the Argosy Casino Baton Rouge remains dockside and
offers its customers unlimited ingress and egress during its hours of operation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
riverboat casino is complemented by a 730-space parking garage, a 270-space surface parking lot and by our adjacent real estate development known as Catfish
Town. Catfish Town is located next to </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>5</FONT></P>

Baton Rouge's convention complex, the Centroplex, which has a 12,000-seat arena and a 30,000-square foot exhibition hall. Catfish Town includes a 50,000 square foot

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Argosy Casino Sioux City  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Argosy Casino Sioux City is located on the Missouri River in downtown Sioux City, Iowa. The riverboat features
12,500 square feet of gaming space, 454 slot machines and 14 table games. The Argosy Casino Sioux City typically conducts one two-hour cruise each day for 100&nbsp;days per year. At all
other times the Argosy Casino Sioux City remains dockside and operates with unlimited ingress and egress. The casino is complemented by adjacent barge facilities featuring buffet dining facilities,
meeting space and administrative support offices. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital Improvements:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 2002, we spent approximately $5.7&nbsp;million in capital expenditures, including
$3.8&nbsp;million on our renovation project of a barge facility that will include a new restaurant,
party/function room and promotions booth, as well as office space for employees. In 2003, we expect to spend approximately $4&nbsp;million in capital improvements, including $2&nbsp;million to
complete the renovation project and $1&nbsp;million on cashless gaming products. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gaming Market:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Argosy Casino Sioux City draws from a population of approximately 80,000 residents in Sioux City and an
estimated 100,000 people within a 40-mile radius of Sioux City. The Argosy Casino Sioux City competes primarily with land-based Native American casinos that are not required to
report gaming revenues and other operating statistics, therefore market comparisons cannot be made. We also compete with certain providers and operators of video gaming in the neighboring state of
South Dakota. Additionally, we compete with slot machines at a pari-mutuel racetrack in Council Bluffs, Iowa and with two riverboat casinos in the Council Bluffs/Omaha, Nebraska market. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulatory Update:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our Iowa gaming license is subject to annual renewal each March. In addition, Iowa law stipulates that a
referendum must be held every eight years to reaffirm gaming in each county that has gaming. This referendum was approved in November&nbsp;2002, thus continuing gaming in the county we operate for
another eight years. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Empress Casino Joliet  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Empress Casino Joliet is located in Joliet, Illinois on a 300-acre site approximately 40 miles
southwest of Chicago. The casino consists of two adjacent riverboat vessels providing a combined 36,066 square feet of gaming space with 1,113 slot machines and 32 table games. Both riverboats remain
dockside and offer customers unlimited ingress and egress. The complex features a 150,000 square foot Egyptian themed pavilion with three restaurants, an entertainment lounge and banquet/conference
facilities. The pavilion also contains an off-track pari-mutuel betting parlor. The complex also includes a 102-room hotel, surface parking areas with approximately
2,350 spaces and an 80-space recreational vehicle park. We acquired 100% of the Empress Casino Joliet as of July&nbsp;31, 2001, for approximately $463.8&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital Improvements:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 2002, we spent approximately $23.0&nbsp;million in capital expenditures, including
$3.6&nbsp;million in maintenance capital and $19.4 on a renovation project which will replace our existing two boats that currently operate a total of five levels of gaming space with a
two-level barge facility that was purchased in 2002. When completed, the barge will offer approximately 50,000 square feet of gaming space, plus an additional 15,000 square feet for a
party room and player's lounge. In 2003, we intend to spend approximately $25&nbsp;million in capital expenditures, including approximately $21&nbsp;million to complete this project and including
$3&nbsp;million on cashless gaming product subject to regulatory approval. This new facility will enhance customer appeal in this competitive market as well as deliver a number of operational
efficiencies at the same time. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Gaming Market:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Empress Casino Joliet draws from a population of approximately 8.0&nbsp;million people who reside within
50 miles of Joliet, including Chicago, which has the largest local population of any state-licensed gaming market and is the third largest gaming market in the United States. The target customers of
the Empress Casino Joliet are drawn largely from the southern and western regions of the greater Chicago metropolitan area, as well as portions of north central Illinois. The eight riverboat casinos
operating in the Chicago market generated approximately $2.1&nbsp;billion of gaming revenues in 2002, a 5.1% increase from 2001. The Empress Casino Joliet had 10.0% of gaming position capacity in
the Chicago market as of December&nbsp;31, 2002, and captured 11.4% of the market's casino revenues in 2002. The competitive impact of dockside gaming in Indiana and facility renovations by two
nearby casinos have resulted in a decrease in the Empress Casino Joliet's market share of approximately 1.5 percentage points from 2001 to 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulatory Update:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Illinois gaming law currently limits the number of gaming licenses to be issued in the state to ten. Each
license permits the operation of up to two boats as part of a single riverboat gaming operation with a combined maximum of 1,200 gaming positions as defined by the state. Our Illinois license for
Joliet was issued at the time of our acquisition of Empress Casino Joliet and was renewed in July&nbsp;2002 for four years. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
June&nbsp;1999, Illinois passed an amendment to the Illinois Riverboat Gambling Act to permit casinos to offer continuous dockside gaming with unlimited ingress and egress. As a
result of litigation challenging certain provisions of the 1999 amendment, dockside gaming could be overturned and we could be required to suspend dockside gaming activities at our Joliet casino until
such time as the Illinois legislature reauthorized dockside gaming. We are unable to determine what the ultimate resolution of the litigation will be; however, the loss of dockside gaming at our
Joliet casino would adversely affect our financial results. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Marketing  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We focus our marketing efforts on direct and relationship marketing to encourage repeat business and foster customer loyalty. We have designed an overall
marketing strategy of utilizing direct marketing as our primary means of communicating with our customers. Although the marketing plan </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>7</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=8,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=889443,FOLIO='7',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DG1898A.;11',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dg1898_1_8"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
for each of our properties is tailored to the specific needs of the site, the common strategic components are: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>further
refine and enhance our database marketing efforts;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>continue
to enhance our full-service player development program to service our most valuable customers;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>aggressively
market our gaming product and facility improvements;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>refine,

<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>utilize

</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A
key tactic in implementing our overall strategy is the effective use of the information we obtain regarding our customers' playing activity. At each of our properties, we encourage
patrons to join the Argosy Preferred Club. We then track the member's level of play through the use of sophisticated player tracking systems. We have placed in service during the fourth quarter 2002,
our integrated data warehouse that expands and refines our knowledge of our customers. Utilizing the information from our databases, we create promotions including targeted direct mail coin offers and
"members only" parties, tournaments, sweepstakes and special entertainment events. This data warehouse stores information on more than two million Argosy Preferred Club members in our marketing
databases, of which active customers account for approximately 60% of our revenues. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Competition  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The U.S. gaming industry is intensely competitive and features many participants, including riverboat casinos, dockside casinos, land-based casinos,
video lottery and poker machines not located in casinos, Native American gaming and other forms of gambling in the United States. Gaming competition is particularly intense in each of the markets
where we operate. Historically, we have been an early entrant in each of our markets; however, as competing properties have opened, our operating results in each of these markets have been negatively
affected. Many of our competitors have more gaming industry experience, are larger and have significantly greater financial and other resources. In addition, some of our direct competitors in certain
markets may have superior facilities and/or operating conditions in terms of: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>amenities
offered at the gaming facility and the related support and entertainment facilities;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>convenient
parking facilities;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
location more favorably situated to the population base of a market and ease of accessibility to the casino site; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>favorable
tax or regulatory factors. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
competitive position of each of our casino properties is discussed in detail in the subsection entitled "Gaming Market" in the "Business&#151;Casino Properties" section of
this 10-K. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There
could be further competition in our markets as a result of the upgrading or expansion of facilities by existing market participants, the entrance of new gaming participants into a
market or
legislative changes. We expect each market, in which we participate, both current and prospective, to be highly competitive. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Employees  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of December&nbsp;31, 2002, we employed approximately 6,130 full-time and 770 part-time employees. The Seafarers Entertainment and
Allied Trade Union represent approximately 2,694 </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>8</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Other Regulatory  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We are subject to certain federal, state and local safety and health laws, regulations and ordinances that apply to non-gaming businesses generally,
such as the Clean Air Act, Clean Water Act, Occupational Safety and Health Act, Resource Conservation Recovery Act and the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation and Liability Act. We have
not made, and do not anticipate making, material expenditures in order to comply with applicable provisions of these laws and regulations. However, the coverage and attendant compliance costs
associated with these laws, regulations and ordinances may result in future additional costs. The Department of Transportation has proposed regulations requiring owners and operators of certain
vessels to establish through the U.S. Coast Guard evidence of financial responsibility in the amount of $5.5&nbsp;million for clean up of oil pollution. This requirement can be satisfied by either
proof of adequate insurance, including self-insurance, or the posting of a surety bond or guaranty. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
riverboats must comply with U.S. Coast Guard requirements as to boat design, on-board facilities, equipment, personnel and safety. Each riverboat must hold a certificate
of seaworthiness or must be approved by the American Bureau of Shipping ("ABS") for stabilization and floatation, and may also be subject to local zoning and building codes. The U.S. Coast Guard
requirements establish design standards, set limits on the operation of the vessels and require individual licensing of all personnel involved with the operation of the vessels. Loss of a vessel's
certificate of seaworthiness or ABS approval would preclude its use as a floating casino. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Permanently
moored vessels are not required to hold certificates of documentation and inspection from the U.S. Coast Guard. However, the permanently moored vessels are inspected by a
third party and certified with respect to stability and single compartment flooding integrity. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our
marine operation employees may be subject to the Jones Act, which, among other things, exempts those employees from the state limits on workers' compensation awards. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulations
adopted by the Financial Crimes Enforcement Network of the U.S. Treasury Department require us to report currency transactions in excess of $10,000 by a single customer
occurring within a gaming day, including identifying the customer by name and social security number. The regulation provides that substantial penalties can be imposed for each instance of a failure
to report. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Insurance  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We carry property and casualty insurance on our land-based assets and our vessels, generally in the amount of their replacement costs, with a nominal
deductible with respect to our land-based assets and a deductible equal to 1% of the replacement value of the vessels. Our land-based assets are covered by flood and earthquake
insurance. Our general liability insurance with respect to land-based operations has a limit of $1&nbsp;million per occurrence and $2&nbsp;million as an annual aggregate with a
$100,000 self-insured retention. Our general liability insurance with respect to our marine operations has a </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>9</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<A NAME="page_dg1898_1_10"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
$100,000 per occurrence self-insured retention with per occurrence coverage up to a $200&nbsp;million limit. With respect to worker's compensation, we have a $250,000 per occurrence
deductible with a $1&nbsp;million per occurrence limit. We carry business interruption insurance policies at our properties, which carry deductibles ranging from 14 to 30&nbsp;days and maximum
coverage up to $62&nbsp;million, depending on the location. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=11,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=809587,FOLIO='10',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DG1898A.;11',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dg1898_1_11"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dg1898_item_3._legal_proceedings"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dg1898_2"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>ITEM 3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LEGAL PROCEEDINGS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We are, from time to time, a party to legal proceedings arising in the ordinary course of business. Other than as disclosed below, we are unaware of any legal
proceedings, which, even if the outcome were unfavorable to us, would have a material adverse impact on either our financial condition or results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Gaming Industry Class Actions  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We have been named, along with two gaming equipment suppliers, 41 of the country's largest gaming operators and four gaming distributors (the "Gaming Industry
Defendants") in three class action lawsuits pending in Las Vegas, Nevada. The suits allege that the Gaming Industry Defendants violated the Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act ("RICO")
by engaging in a course of fraudulent and misleading conduct intended to induce people to play their gaming machines based upon a false belief concerning how those gaming machines actually operate, as
well as to the extent to which there is actually an opportunity to win on any given play. The suits seek unspecified compensatory and punitive damages. On January&nbsp;14, 1997, the court
consolidated all three actions under the case name </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>William H. Poulos, etc. v. Caesars World,&nbsp;Inc., et al.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> On February&nbsp;13, 1997, the
plaintiffs filed a consolidated amended complaint. The court subsequently dismissed this complaint, in part, and on January&nbsp;8, 1998, the plaintiffs filed a second amended complaint. The parties
have fully briefed the plaintiff's motion for class certification. The court held a hearing on this motion on November&nbsp;15, 2001. The parties are awaiting a decision from the court. Discovery
has been stayed pending the court's ruling. We are unable to determine what effect, if any, the suit would have on our business or operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Conservancy District Lease Litigation in Dearborn County, Indiana  </I></B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On March&nbsp;21, 1997, Deborah S. Whitacre filed an action in the Circuit Court of Dearborn County, Indiana as Cause
No.&nbsp;15CO1-9703-CP-073, challenging the validity of a lease to the City by the Conservancy District of Lawrenceburg, Indiana (the "District") of certain land
owned by the District, which land has in turn been subleased by the City to our affiliate Indiana Gaming, L.P. and is being used for development and operation of the riverboat gaming facility in the
City for which Indiana Gaming, L.P. has been awarded a riverboat owner's license by the Indiana Gaming Commission. Defendants are the District and its individual directors. In 1998, Indiana Gaming,
L.P. was permitted to intervene and is now contesting the action. The District and its directors have advised that they are contesting the action and intend to continue to do so. An adverse ruling in
this matter could have a material adverse effect on our financial condition and results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Capitol House Preservation Company, L.L.C. v. Jazz Enterprises,&nbsp;Inc. et. al.  </I></B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On November&nbsp;26, 1997, Capitol House filed an amended petition in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for East Baton Rouge Parish, State of Louisiana, on
November&nbsp;26, 1997, amending its previously filed but unserved suit against Richard Perryman, the person selected by the Louisiana Gaming Division to evaluate and rank the applicants seeking a
gaming license for East Baton Rouge Parish, and now adding its state law claims against Jazz, the Former Jazz Shareholders, Argosy Gaming Company, Argosy of Louisiana,&nbsp;Inc. and Catfish Queen
Partnership in Commendam, d/b/a the Belle of Baton Rouge Casino. This suit alleges that these parties violated the Louisiana Unfair Trade Practices Act in connection with obtaining the gaming license
that was issued to us. The defendants have filed exceptions which contest the right of Capitol House to attack in this lawsuit the final decision of the Louisiana Gaming Enforcement Division in
granting a gaming license to the defendants and denying the license to Capitol House. The trial court overruled the defendants' exceptions, but the defendants have applied to the Louisiana First
Circuit Court of Appeal for a writ of review. The Louisiana First Circuit Court of Appeal denied defendant's writ application and therefore the defendants have now </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>11</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=12,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=809473,FOLIO='11',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DG1898A.;11',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dg1898_1_12"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
again appealed to the Louisiana Supreme Court. If the First Circuit grants the writ and rules in favor of the defendants, the claims of Capitol House will be dismissed. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
intend to seek indemnification from the Former Jazz Shareholders for any liability we, Argosy Louisiana or Jazz suffers as a result of such cause of action. As part of the
consideration payable by us to the Former Jazz Shareholders for the acquisition of Jazz, we agreed at the time of such acquisition to annual deferred purchase price payments of $1,350,000 for each of
the first ten years after closing and $500,000 for each of the next ten years. Payments are to be made quarterly by us. The definitive acquisition documents provide us with offset rights against such
deferred purchase price payments for indemnification claims against the Former Jazz Shareholders and for liabilities that the Former Jazz Shareholders contractually agreed to retain. There can be no
assurance that the Former Jazz Shareholders will have assets sufficient to satisfy any claim in excess of our offset rights, therefore, an adverse ruling in this matter could have a material adverse
effect on us. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
March 17, 2003, the reported last sales price for the Common Stock was $17.95. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Since
our initial public offering in February&nbsp;1993, we have not declared any cash dividends or distributions on our Common Stock. Although we currently intend to retain our
earnings to finance future growth and therefore have no present intention of paying dividends, this policy will be reviewed quarterly by our Board of Directors in light of, among other things, our
results of operations, capital requirements, any restrictions imposed by applicable gaming regulations and restrictions imposed by our indentures and loan documents. At present, our Amended and
Restated Credit Agreement dated July&nbsp;31, 2001, requires the consent of the lenders in order to declare a dividend. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="di1898_item_7._management_s_discussio__ite03668"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_di1898_4"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>ITEM 7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MANAGEMENT'S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="di1898_argosy_gaming_company_manageme__arg04368"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_di1898_5"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY<BR>  MANAGEMENT'S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS<BR>  OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as otherwise noted, the words "we", "us", "our" and similar terms, as well as references to "Argosy" or the "Company" refer to Argosy Gaming Company and
all of its subsidiaries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Cautionary Statements for Purposes of the "Safe Harbor" Provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>This Report contains forward-looking statements within the meaning of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995. When used in
this document, the words "anticipate," "believe," "estimate" and "expect" and similar expressions are generally intended to identify forward-looking statements. Investors are cautioned that any
forward-looking statements, including those regarding the intent, belief or current expectations of the Company or its management, are not guarantees of future performance and involve risks and
uncertainties, and that actual results may differ materially from those in the forward-looking statements as a result of various factors including, but not limited to, (i)&nbsp;construction delays
related to the Company's expansion projects' (ii)&nbsp;competitive and general economic conditions in the markets in which the Company operates, (iii)&nbsp;the effect of future legislation or
regulatory changes on the Company's operations, including but not limited to gaming tax increases, issuances of additional gaming licenses and the approval of cashless slots, and (iv)&nbsp;other
risks detailed from time to time in the Company's Securities and Exchange Commission filings. The Company does not intend to update these forward-looking statements.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Overview  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We own and operate the Alton Belle Casino in Alton, Illinois; the Empress Casino Joliet in Joliet, Illinois; the Argosy Casino in Riverside, Missouri; the Argosy
Casino in Baton Rouge, Louisiana; the Argosy Casino in Sioux City, Iowa; and the Argosy Casino in Lawrenceburg, Indiana. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
2002, many factors affected our casinos' operations. Effective August&nbsp;1, 2002, our Lawrenceburg casino commenced dockside gaming. This has had a positive impact on casino
revenues in the last half of 2002. During the second quarter 2002, Illinois and Indiana enacted legislation increasing gaming tax rates. Also, in late 2001 and 2002, three competitors made significant
renovations, which, coupled with the increased gaming tax rates, have negatively impacted our Alton and Joliet, Illinois casino operations. In addition, dockside gaming in Indiana has negatively
impacted our Joliet, Illinois casino operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
the first quarter 2001, we acquired the minority interests in our Argosy Casino in Lawrenceburg, Indiana. Following the acquisition of these minority interests, we now own 100% of
all our operations and are no longer required to record minority interest expense. On July&nbsp;31, 2001, we acquired the Empress Casino Joliet in Joliet, Illinois. The results of our operations for
2001 include the results of Empress Casino Joliet for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. </FONT></P>

<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>(3)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Includes
operations of Jazz Enterprises,&nbsp;Inc., a wholly owned subsidiary that owns and operates the Catfish Town real estate development adjacent to our Baton Rouge casino.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>(4)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, includes a $1.9&nbsp;million pretax charge related to the abandonment of a proposed casino in Kenosha, Wisconsin. The year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000, includes a $6.8&nbsp;million pretax charge related to the write-down of the Alton landing facility.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>(5)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>"EBITDA"
is defined as earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization and is presented before any management fees paid to Argosy. EBITDA should not be construed as an
alternative to financial measures determined in accordance with generally accepted accounting
principles, such as income from operations, net income, or cash flows generated by operating, investing and financing activities. EBITDA is presented solely as a supplemental disclosure because
management believes that it is a widely used measure of operating performance in the gaming industry and for companies with a significant amount of depreciation and amortization. EBITDA may not be
comparable to similarly titled measures reported by other companies. We have other significant uses of cash flows, including debt service and capital expenditures, which are not reflected in EBITDA. A
reconciliation from EBITDA to Income from operations is as follows: </FONT></DD></DL>

NAME="page_dk1898_1_18"> </A> </FONT></P>

<!-- TOC_END -->

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, compared to year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Casino</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Casino revenues for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, increased $161.3&nbsp;million,
or 20.6%, to $944.7&nbsp;million from $783.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Lawrenceburg casino revenues increased $27.3&nbsp;million, or 7.9%, to
$373.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $346.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Lawrenceburg commenced dockside gaming on August&nbsp;1,
2002. The Empress Casino Joliet recorded $237.6&nbsp;million of casino revenue for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, compared to $102.1&nbsp;million in casino revenue for the five months
since acquisition (July&nbsp;31, 2001) through December&nbsp;31, 2001. The competitive impact of dockside gaming in Indiana and facility renovations by two nearby casinos have resulted in a
decrease in Joliet's casino revenues of $8.9&nbsp;million, from the $102.1&nbsp;million for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, to $93.2&nbsp;million for the five months ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002. Alton, Riverside, Sioux City and Baton Rouge 2002 casino revenues remained relatively constant, decreasing from $334.9&nbsp;million to $333.4&nbsp;million. Increased
competitive pressures due to an expanded facility by a competitor in August&nbsp;2002 affected our Alton casino. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Casino
expenses increased $100.0&nbsp;million to $432.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $332.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31,
2001. Joliet incurred $124.4&nbsp;million in casino expenses for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, and $48.3&nbsp;million for the five months of operations from our acquisition through
December&nbsp;31, 2001, a $76.1&nbsp;million increase. Joliet's casino expenses for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, were $47.6&nbsp;million, a $0.7&nbsp;million decrease
compared to the five months of operations from our purchase through December&nbsp;31, 2001. The remaining increase is due primarily to increased gaming taxes of $23.7&nbsp;million at our
Lawrenceburg casino corresponding to an increase in revenue with dockside gaming and an increase in gaming tax rates. Based on 2002 casino revenues, our casino expense would have been approximately
$33&nbsp;million lower in 2002 without the changes in gaming tax rates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Admissions</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Admissions revenues (net of complimentary admissions) decreased to $1.9&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $3.3&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. This reduction is due primarily to a reduction in the admissions price during 2002 at Lawrenceburg. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Food, Beverage and Other</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Food, beverage and other revenues increased from $82.1&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2001, to $97.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002. Joliet contributed $11.9&nbsp;million of this increase in food, beverage and other revenue. Food,
beverage and other net profit improved $4.9&nbsp;million to $25.3&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002. Of the increase, Joliet and
Baton Rouge (including hotel operations) contributed $3.0&nbsp;million and $1.6&nbsp;million, respectively, of this net profit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Selling, General and Administrative</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased $14.9&nbsp;million from
$118.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, to $133.6&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, due primarily to a $7.5&nbsp;million increase in Joliet's
expenses to $15.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $8.2&nbsp;million for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. The remaining increase is due primarily to an
increase of $4.1&nbsp;million in city development fees in Lawrenceburg due to the increase in revenues related to the commencement of dockside gaming effective August&nbsp;1, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Other Operating Expenses</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Other operating expenses increased by $4.6&nbsp;million to $40.9&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002, as compared to $36.3&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Joliet incurred $10.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002 and
$4.2&nbsp;million for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Other operating expenses in 2001 include a charge of $1.9&nbsp;million relating to the abandonment of the proposed Kenosha
casino development. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Depreciation and amortization increased $0.1&nbsp;million to $47.4&nbsp;million for the year
ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $47.3&nbsp;million in 2001. Joliet's expense </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>18</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=19,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=533296,FOLIO='18',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DK1898A.;10',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1898_1_19"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
increased $5.9&nbsp;million from $4.0&nbsp;million for the five months ended December&nbsp;31, 2001 to $9.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002. Depreciation expense also
increased due to accelerated depreciation of $0.6&nbsp;million on planned asset retirements and $0.5&nbsp;million on our new data warehouse placed in service during the third quarter 2002. These
increases are offset by no longer amortizing goodwill in 2002 in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;142 "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets," effective January&nbsp;1, 2002. If SFAS&nbsp;142 had
been in effect January&nbsp;1, 2001, pre-tax goodwill amortization of $7.8&nbsp;million would not have been recorded for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. All goodwill is
subject to impairment testing at least annually. Based on our evaluations performed during 2002, we have no impairment to record. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Interest Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net interest expense increased $14.4&nbsp;million to $81.2&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002, from $66.8&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. This increase is primarily attributable to additional borrowings in connection with the Lawrenceburg
and Joliet acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Minority Interests</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;We had no minority interest expense for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, as compared to
$4.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. This decrease is attributable to our Lawrenceburg casino minority interest acquisitions during the first quarter of 2001. As the sole
owner, we no longer incur minority interest expense. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Income Tax Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;We recorded income tax expense of $57.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002,
compared to income tax expense of $46.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, due to increased pretax earnings and an increase in our effective corporate income tax rate due to
an increase in Indiana tax rates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net income was $71.5&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, compared to $66.1&nbsp;million
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, due primarily to the factors discussed above. If SFAS&nbsp;142 had been in effect January&nbsp;1, 2001, our net income would have increased by
$4.6&nbsp;million to $70.7&nbsp;million and our diluted net income per share would have increased by $0.16 to $2.41 for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, compared to year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Casino</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Casino revenues for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, increased $124.5&nbsp;million,
or 18.9% to $783.4&nbsp;million from $658.9&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. Alton, Riverside, Sioux City and Baton Rouge reported an aggregate 6.4% increase in casino
revenues from $314.9&nbsp;million to $334.9&nbsp;million. Lawrenceburg casino revenues increased $2.4&nbsp;million, or 0.7% to $346.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001,
from $344.0&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. The Empress Casino Joliet, acquired July&nbsp;31, 2001, recorded $102.1&nbsp;million in casino revenue for the five months
since acquisition through December&nbsp;31, 2001. Each of our casinos reported increases in average win per passenger for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, versus the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Casino
expenses increased 22.1% to $332.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, from $272.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. Joliet
incurred $48.3&nbsp;million in casino expenses during the five months of operations since our acquisition. The remaining increase is due to increased gaming taxes totaling $7.5&nbsp;million and
increases in other casino expenses, primarily payroll related, of $4.2&nbsp;million to support the overall increased revenues. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Admissions</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Admissions revenues (net of complimentary admissions) were $3.3&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2001, compared to $6.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. This reduction is due to an increase in complimentary admissions given to customers as part of
Lawrenceburg's marketing program in response to increased competition. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT

December&nbsp;31, 2000, to $82.1&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Joliet contributed $9.5&nbsp;million of this increase in food, beverage and other revenue. Food,
beverage and other net profit improved $0.9&nbsp;million to $20.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Joliet contributed $1.5&nbsp;million of this net profit, offset by
small reductions in net profit at other properties. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Selling, General and Administrative</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased 10.7% from $107.2&nbsp;million
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, to $118.7&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001. Joliet had $8.2&nbsp;million in selling, general and administrative expenses. The
remaining increase is due to increased costs associated with the overall increase in revenues at all of our other properties. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Other Operating Expenses</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Other operating expenses increased by $6.1&nbsp;million to $36.3&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2001, as compared to $30.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000. Joliet accounted for $4.2&nbsp;million of the increase with the remaining portion of the
increase due to the write-off of the proposed Kenosha casino development. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Depreciation and amortization increased $11.2&nbsp;million to $47.3&nbsp;million for the
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, from $36.1&nbsp;million in 2000. This increase is primarily due to the $6.6&nbsp;million in incremental goodwill amortization related to the Lawrenceburg
acquisition during the first quarter of 2001 and depreciation and intangible amortization expense of $4.0&nbsp;million resulting from the Joliet acquisition on July&nbsp;31, 2001. In accordance
with SFAS No.&nbsp;142 "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets," effective January&nbsp;1, 2002, we will no longer amortize our goodwill. All goodwill will be subject to impairment testing at least
annually. Pre-tax goodwill amortization expense for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001 would have decreased by $7.8&nbsp;million had SFAS No.&nbsp;142 been effective for 2001 for
goodwill acquired prior to July&nbsp;1, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Interest Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net interest expense increased $33.4&nbsp;million to $66.8&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2001. This increase is primarily attributable to additional borrowings in connection with the Lawrenceburg and Joliet acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Minority Interests</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Our minority interest expense decreased by $36.4&nbsp;million to $4.1&nbsp;million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2001. This decrease is attributable to our Lawrenceburg casino minority interest acquisitions during the first quarter of 2001. As the sole owner, we no longer incur minority
interest expense. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Income Tax Expense</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;We recorded income tax expense of $46.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001,
compared to income tax expense of $31.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, due to increased pretax earnings, net of minority interest expense. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Extraordinary Loss</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;We recorded an extraordinary loss of $1.2&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000,
related to completion of the final phase of the 1999 refinancing. This extraordinary loss is net of a $0.8&nbsp;million tax benefit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT><FONT
SIZE=2><I>Net Income Attributable to Common Stockholders</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;Net income attributable to common stockholders was $66.1&nbsp;million for the
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2001, compared to $45.4&nbsp;million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2000, due primarily to the factors discussed above. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During 2002, we generated cash flows from operating activities of $165.6&nbsp;million compared to $138.5&nbsp;million for 2001. This increase is attributable
to our increase in operating income of $26.9&nbsp;million, an increase in our cash flow from working capital of $10.4&nbsp;million throughout our properties, offset by an increase in interest
expense of $13.7&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>20</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=21,EFW="2105122",CP="ARGOSY GAMING COMPANY",DN="1",CHK=973679,FOLIO='20',FILE='DISK006:[03CHI8.03CHI1898]DK1898A.;10',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='25-MAR-2003;13:09' -->
<A NAME="page_dk1898_1_21"> </A>
<BR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2002, we used cash flows for investing activities of $56.3&nbsp;million versus $848.3&nbsp;million for 2001. During 2002, our investing activities included
$56.7&nbsp;million for purchases of property and equipment, a $26.5&nbsp;million increase over our property and equipment purchases in 2001. This increase is due primarily to construction and
expansion projects at our Joliet, Sioux City and Riverside facilities, plus renovation at our Baton Rouge casino. Capital expenditures in 2002 consisted of $23.1&nbsp;million in maintenance capital
and $33.6&nbsp;million in project capital, primarily for the expansion projects mentioned above. 2001 includes $366.7&nbsp;million and $451.6&nbsp;million used for the purchase of the minority
interests in Lawrenceburg and the acquisition of the Empress Casino Joliet, respectively. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2002, we used $106.8&nbsp;million in financing activities compared to providing $707.6&nbsp;million in cash flows from financing activities in 2001. During 2002, we paid down
$103.9&nbsp;million on our revolving Credit Facility. During 2001, we received proceeds of $748.8&nbsp;million through the issuance of Subordinated Notes and borrowings under our Credit Facility.
We used these funds for the purchase of the Lawrenceburg minority interests and our acquisition of the Empress Casino Joliet. Also during 2001, we spent $20.6&nbsp;million in financing fees related
to the Lawrenceburg and Empress Casino Joliet acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At
December&nbsp;31, 2002, we had approximately $59.7&nbsp;million of cash and cash equivalents. At December&nbsp;31, 2002, we had outstanding $329.2&nbsp;million on our Senior
Secured Credit Facility ($58.3&nbsp;million on our revolving Credit Facility and $270.9&nbsp;million on our Term Loan) and $557.5&nbsp;million of Subordinated Notes (due in June&nbsp;2009 and
September&nbsp;2011), including $7.5&nbsp;million of unamortized premium. As of December&nbsp;31, 2002, we had outstanding letters of credit of $7.5&nbsp;million. As of February&nbsp;20,
2003, availability under the Credit Facility was approximately $183.8&nbsp;million. We have no off balance sheet debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Subordinated Notes and Credit Facility contain certain restrictions on the payment of dividends on our common stock and the occurrence of additional indebtedness, as well as other
typical debt
covenants. In addition, the Credit Facility requires us to maintain certain financial ratios as follows: (1)&nbsp;Total Funded Debt to EBITDA Ratio of a maximum of 4.25 to 1.0; (2)&nbsp;Senior
Leverage Ratio of a maximum of 2.50 to 1.0; (3)&nbsp;Fixed Charge Ratio of a minimum of 1.25 to 1.0. As of December&nbsp;31, 2002, we are in compliance with these ratios. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
have made a significant investment in property and equipment and plan to make significant additional investments at our existing properties. In 2002, we have begun construction on
major projects at our Riverside, Joliet and Sioux City properties. We have spent approximately $10.1&nbsp;million, $19.4&nbsp;million and $3.8&nbsp;million, respectively, in 2002 on these
renovations. In 2003, we expect to spend approximately $115&nbsp;million to complete these projects. In addition, we expect maintenance capital expenditures primarily related to the purchase of new
cashless gaming product and facility enhancements to be approximately $40&nbsp;million in 2003. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Consistent
with gaming industry practice, we conduct our operations with a net working capital deficit. Unlike traditional industrial companies, a gaming company's balance sheet has
limited accounts receivable and inventories. In addition, casinos generate significant cash on a daily basis. We generally apply our daily cash flows to pay down indebtedness under our revolving
Credit Facility and pay our current liabilities pursuant to their normal cycles. Given the significant daily cash flows generated by our operations and the financial flexibility provided by our Credit
Facility, the existence of a working capital deficit has no impact on our ability to operate our business or meet our obligations as they become due. We believe that cash on hand, operating cash flows
and funds available under our Credit Facility will be sufficient to fund our current operating, capital expenditure and debt service obligations for the next 12&nbsp;months. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>21</FONT></P>
